< text>
What a great experience! I booked online (12 people max per time slot), and noticed that sometimes there are discounts for last-minute bookings / early departures (e.g., 9 AM).

The check-in office is located to the left of the Deli on the second floor.
Take off and landing are done at the back of the boat, and one does not typically get wet (except maybe a quick feet dip during landing).

The flight time for us lasted about 10 minutes for each pair. I recommend getting the 800ft package, because the views up there are pretty amazing. Make sure to bring some cash to tip the guides as they do a fantastic job of keeping things safe and moving on time.

Caution: The boat ride can get pretty rough, but they do provide barf bags onboard :)</text>

< text>
Five stars because our room and amenities exceeded my expectations. First of all, my husband and I stayed two nights here with our 14 month old son to celebrate our second anniversary and they provided a *clean* pack and play/crib for our boy! That meant so much to me... we were going to let him sleep with us but thankfully we were able to enjoy our nights together here. The location is about 1.5 hours from the entrance to Sequoia National Park but I would have rather stayed at Rio Sierra instead of gone to see the big trees.

The river was SO much fun. To anyone with kids, I was surprised to see that some previous guests layed out rocks near the shore to create two 'kiddie pools' which allowed our son to have fun and let us feel more secure about having him in the river.

A few things I adored were all of the private and relaxing spots to sit down in the shade or even in a hammock. The towels provided were large and soft, easy to find and smelled like honey, oh my they smelled SO GOOD. Mars seemed to have a green thumb (like myself) so I REALLY loved what she did/does with the place. She has utilized every inch of that place to grow gorgeous foliage/flowers.

Our room was gorgeous and inviting. I felt very comfortable and the shower/tub had a giant moon light above it and a large potted plant sitting on the tile beneath the light. I will include a photo. What a romantic bathroom with more than a few night light/lamps and plenty of counter space. We had breakfast once made by Deborah($15) and once made by Mars($10) and although Mars was smaller, and they were both healthy and wholesome. You can make special requests ahead of time by texting Mars.

In closing I would like to mention how kind and well spoken Mars is. I was coming around a corner to get something from our room when I was greeted by Mars big smile, hand on her hip, asking, "are you my guest?". She was kind enough to unexpectedly serve us ice cold hibiscus tea while we were relaxing under the shade after a swim. She answered all of my questions and even told us the detailed story of how she acquired Rio Sierra, who built it, etc. The house was already charming but that just added to it.

In closing, I have a few cons to note for future guests. If you or anyone you are staying with is a light sleeper, be aware of the squeaky old wood flooring. I grew up in a house with squeaky wood flooring so although it was nostalgic, it made walking to the bathroom with a sleeping baby in the room quite a mission. Also, our bed was comfortable (especially the pillows) but squeaky as well. If you are afraid of lizards, they are everywhere. It really gives the place more character. I love reptiles but I also know some scaredy cats.

My last comment is on a charge we had after we left the river house. We were confused about a 'room cleaning fee' of $25 so I gave Mars a call simply to ask if we had made a mess or something of the sort. I had never seen a separate charge for a room cleaning. Mars explained why they do it that way and quickly offered to credit us back the $25. How sweet of her! We just cannot wait to go back to Rio Sierra!<//text>

<rating>5</rating>< text>
Cabrillo is a great community college with many AA/AS degrees as well as certificate programs.  The Culinary Arts programs is awesome with a the Pino Alto Restaurant as a place for the students to cook with their professional teachers and be rated by the public.  The catering class even gives the students experiences catering weddings by being a part of the front and back of the house.

The Cabrillo Summer Youth Programs are great for kids. My daughter enjoyed the computer class in which they put together computers/ or fixed and then added software to make the computer or laptop usable.

The Cabrillo Youth Chorus om the college campus and taught by the college choir director is excellent. The chorus gets invites to Carnegie Hall and other places because of their excellent reputation and quality singing by the young people.  It is a great program to learn about music reading, solfege,  rounds and sing a variety of music - classics, musicals, foreign language songs, etc.<//text>

<user_name>Naoshi Pfeffer< /user_name><Date>1618112924664<//Date><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
An amazing gem toughing it out in the heart of the city.

The interior, with it's chairs stacked and tables lining the walls as if barricading an imminent attack, shows artifacts of authentic japanese ambiance that deserves to be enjoyed.

Unfortunate that we are still confronted with our collective challenge, 'Kushu Ramen' embodies that quiet strength needed to survive. Like an old western, a shootout in the saloon, I hope to see this movie end with our heroes having the last laugh.

I'll look forward for what the future brings to this charming area. As a community, we need to help each other to get us better than where we were. I say thank you, for all you do and will do.</Review>

The first time I came to this place was during my college days a few years ago. The place hasn't changed much, the menu hasn't changed much either, just the food flavor has changed. < Review>
Kyushu Ramen in Van Nuys was the first restaurant we went to after a 2 week trip in Japan‚Ä¶we were in the mood to extend our trip locally and this place is right around the corner from where we live.

We‚Äôre all vegetarians and were happy that they had options for us, though in practice it‚Äôs fairly limited what is available. We ordered 3 vegan ramens, one with spinach noodles (for my gluten free wife) and 2 with regular noodles. The menu didn‚Äôt quite match what was actually brought to us (it was missing the yam cake displayed on the menu. They told us after they brought it that they were out of that item. Lesson 1 or 2 for restaurant people: Let people know about changes before you put them down in front of your diners‚Ä¶we like to be served what we actually order.

Besides that, the ramen had lots of flavor. It was a creamy style miso broth, though it had limited extra ingredients.

We were happy generally with the flavor but would have liked more of the additional ingredients in the bowl.

We might try it again but there are plenty of ramen places in L.A. so it probably won‚Äôt be our first choice after this experience.<//Review>

<Time>1549222182597</Time><Gmap_id>0x80c29746bae330d3:0x8191e11ecfc0a503</Gmap_id><Rating>5< /Rating><user>112628264193355675722</user><response>None<//response></record></dataset><record>
< Review>
The place is relatively full at all times and kinda understaffed. There were only two servers and they truly were giving it their all. They both had a very nice and kind attitude despite of the fact that the overwhelming amount of work might have been too much for just two of them.

The place itself is clean and tidy. It has that typical japanese vibe and the decor and ambiance are reminiscing of any mom and pop japanese restaurant/shop.

The food is delicious and highly recommended. I had the Pork Cutlet bowl and so did my friend and we finished it in record time.

Highly recommended place to come if you don't mind the wait time (no chairs, host/hostess or lounge area, you just have to stand at the entrance and wait till one of the servers notices you, which might take several minutes) and you like excellent japanese food.< /Review>

This is not the first time I've had a negative experience with this restaurant, there have been several in fact.

<date>1553329996119<//date>< rating>
5< /rating>
< review>
Kyushu is that hole in the wall type of place you find when trying to find a restaurant that's open past midnight.

Servers are always friendly, variety is good, and it's pretty well priced. Wait times are sometimes an issue because lines do amass on weekends and Fridays, but dining wait times aren't bad at all.

Their ramen, takoyaki, katsu, and sushi are all great. The Hanabishi box and sushi boat are gimmicky orders but they are worth the price you pay for the amount of food and experience you get in my opinion.

I've never had any bad experiences there. Definitely recommend to anyone, especially late night diners.< /review>

<review>I went here tonight for the first time. Good hosts but the place is very small. You are basically shoulder to shoulder with the people to the next table. They have a sushi bar there as well that takes up a lot of room. The place is divided by a wall. One side, where the entrance is located, has table booths more suitable for privacy and chat with friends, up to 4 people. It has a wall in between which divides the sushi bar and these booth tables. The area with the sushi bar has two people tables so you are forced to sit in front of the person you are with. I went here with my girl friend and I enjoy sitting next to her rather then in front. In addition to the sitting arrangements, the food was decent. I ordered Spicy pork ramen which took my taste buds a minute to get use to. I was not able to figure out this flavor I kept on tasting with ever zip of the spicy broth. The noodles where very chewy and the texture of doe was really out there. Pork was soft but all together it created a flavor I was not to fond of. In conclusion, i do recommend this place if you want a quick bite of either sushi or ramen. They have a variety of liquor, which am sure would of made me enjoy the place a lot more if I drank a bottle to myself. Good luck and enjoy.< /review>< Pics>

<Rating>5</Rating><text>Kyushu is that hole in the wall type of place you find when trying to find a restaurant that's open past midnight.

Servers are always friendly, variety is good, and it's pretty well priced. Wait times are sometimes an issue because lines do amass on weekends and Fridays, but dining wait times aren't bad at all.

Their ramen, takoyaki, katsu, and sushi are all great. The Hanabishi box and sushi boat are gimmicky orders but they are worth the price you pay for the amount of food and experience you get in my opinion.

I've never had any bad experiences there. Definitely recommend to anyone, especially late night diners.</text></record>

< text>
On the day we stopped at Kyushu Ramen... I had a major craving for ramen. Kyushu was a restaurant that is hidden in the San Fernando Valley area. It is a small place with no major catching signs. When we arrived there was a line which to me was a great sign. We waited around 15 minutes for a table of three which was surprisingly fast. When we entered the restaurant it felt very lively, but crowded. Kyushu has a great menu of sushi and ramen. Because of my craving for ramen I only choose ramen. It was the bomb! The broth was delicious and very memorable for me. I have saved Kyushu's location on my google map so when I am in town... i will surely visit it again.< /text>

Then 3 booths all opened up and she still would not let us move without starting the whole process all over again.  This was utterly ridiculous - she said sorry it's our policy.  We ordered the Hanabishi box again, she never brought us a spoon for our soup, then they completely left out the shrimp tempura.  So we waived the lady who brought our food to us and mentioned that there is supposed to be shrimp tempura with this dish, she said she will check the menu. She brings me the menu to let me know it doesn't come with it, but we pointed out that the photo clearly shows two shrimp tempura, so she said she will check with the manager.  Finally, another lady brought two measly shrimp tempura.  The salad was wilty and warm, the soup was cold, the tempura was cold... Also the table where we sat there was a glaring white light right in our eyes, we mentioned this to our waitress and she told us to move to the hard chairs on the other side of the table instead of the bench we were sitting on so we don't have to see the bright light. She said she will turn down the lights - but she never did.  Also when people were seated to the booth next to us, the whole bench was rocking and creaking, and the guy sitting next to me couldn't stop shaking his legs, so we were also bouncing on our bench.  This was one of the worst dining experience, so now we didn't have hair in our food but everything else was truly TERRIBLE!   GO SOMEWHERE ELSE if you want an enjoyable dining experience with better service and food.</Review>< gmap_id>
